Networks)\u3068\u547c\u3070\u308c\u308b\u3002\n\u3055\u3089\u306b\u3001\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf\u3068\u4e26\u884c\u3057\u3066\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u69cb\u9020\u3092\u9032\u5316\u3055\u305b\u308b\u624b\u6cd5\uff08\u4f8b\uff1asynaptic weights\uff09\u3068\u305d\u308c\u3089\u3092\u5225\u3005\u306b\u958b\u767a\u3059\u308b\u624b\u6cd5\u306e\u9055\u3044\u304c\u3042\u308b\u3002\n\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u76f4\u63a5\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\u3068\u9593\u63a5\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\n\u76f4\u63a5\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\u306f\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u3059\u3079\u3066\u306e\u7d50\u5408\u3068\u30ce\u30fc\u30c9\u3092\u907a\u4f1d\u5b50\u3068\u3057\u3066\u67d3\u8272\u4f53\u306b\u8a18\u8ff0\u3059\u308b\u3002\n\u5bfe\u7167\u7684\u306b\u9593\u63a5\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\u306f\u305f\u3044\u3066\u3044\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u3092\u69cb\u6210\u3059\u308b\u30eb\u30fc\u30eb\u3092\u8a18\u8ff0\u3059\u308b\u306e\u307f\u3067\u3042\u308b[2][3]\u3002\n\nDQN ( Deep Q-learning ) \u306e\u540d \u3092 \u4e16\u306b\u77e5\u3089\u3057\u3081\u305f Atari \u30b2\u30fc\u30e0 \u3092 \u30d7\u30ec\u30a4\u3055\u305b\u308b\u8ad6\u6587 \u3082\u3042\u308b\n\nMatthew Hausknecht, Joel Lehman, Risto Miikkulainen, and Peter Stone, A Neuroevolution Approach to General Atari Game Playin\n\n\nThis article addresses the challenge of learning to play many different video games with little domainspecific knowledge.\nSpecifically, it introduces a neuro-evolution approach to general Atari 2600 game playing.\nFour neuro-evolution algorithms were paired with three different state representations and evaluated on a set of 61 Atari games.\nThe neuro-evolution agents represent different points along the spectrum of algorithmic sophistication - including weight evolution on topologically fixed neural networks (Conventional Neuro-evolution), Covariance Matrix Adaptation Evolution Strategy (CMA-ES),\nevolution of network topology and weights (NEAT), and indirect network encoding (HyperNEAT).\nState representations include an object representation of the game screen, the raw pixels of the game screen, and seeded noise (a comparative baseline). \nResults indicate that direct-encoding methods work best on compact state representations while indirect-encoding methods (i.e. HyperNEAT) allow scaling to higher-dimensional representations (i.e. the raw game screen).\nPrevious approaches based on temporaldifference learning had trouble dealing with the large state spaces and sparse reward gradients often found in Atari games.\nNeuro-evolution ameliorates these problems and evolved policies achieve state-of-the-art\nresults, even surpassing human high scores on three games.\nThese results suggest that neuro-evolution is a promising approach to general video game playing.\n\n\nPython \u3092 \u306f\u3058\u3081\u3001\u5404\u8a00\u8a9e\u306e\u30e9\u30a4\u30d6\u30e9\u30ea \u304c \u3059\u3067\u306b \u5229\u7528\u53ef\u80fd\n\n\uff08 Python \uff09\n\nNEAT Java (JNEAT)\n\n\nReleased 2002\nThe JNEAT package contains Java source code for the NeuroEvolution of >Augmenting Topologies method (see the original NEAT C++ package).\nIt includes a nice GUI (see  screenshots ), and implementations of experiments for XOR and 3-bit parity. \nFor answers to common questions, refer to our  FAQ .\nJNEAT was written by Ugo Vierucci based on the original C++ package by Kenneth Stanley. \n\nVersions:\n v1.2 6/24/02 vierucci\n\nANJI (Another NEAT Java Implementation)\n\n\nANJI (Another NEAT Java Implementation)\nBuilt on top of existing OpenSource projects, ANJI is an implementation of NEAT (Neuro-Evolution of Augmenting Topologies), an algorithm for evolving artificial neural networks developed by Kenneth Stanley, working in the Neural Networks Research Group at the University of Texas at Austin.\n\n\uff08 Erlang \uff09\n\nGene I. Angeline, Gregory M. Saunders and Jordan B. Pollack, An Evolutionary Algorithm that Constructs\nRecurrent Neural Networks\n\n\nAbstract\nStandard methods for inducing both the structure and weight values of recurrent neural networks fit an assumed class of architectures to every task. >\nThis simplification is necessary because the interactions between network structure and function are not well understood.\nEvolutionary computation, which includes genetic algorithms and evolutionary programming, is a population-based search method that has shown promise in such complex tasks.\nThis paper argues that genetic algorithms are inappropriate for network acquisition and describes an evolutionary program, called GNARL, that simultaneously acquires both the structure and weights for recurrent networks.\nThis algorithm\u2019s empirical acquisition method allows for the emergence of complex behaviors and topologies that are potentially excluded by the artificial architectural constraints imposed in standard network induction methods.\n\n\nNeuroEvolution \u3092 \u63a1\u7528\u3059\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3067\u3001\u904a\u3079\u3070\u904a\u3076\u307b\u3069\u30b2\u30fc\u30e0\u30ad\u30e3\u30e9\u30af\u30bf\u30fc \u304c \u8ce2\u304f\u632f\u308b\u821e\u3046\u3088\u3046\u306b\u306a\u308b \u30c6\u30ec\u30d3\u30b2\u30fc\u30e0 \u306e \u5b9f\u88c5\u3092 \u63d0\u6848\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b \u8ad6\u6587\n\n\nKenneth O. M. MacCallum, Matthias Mauchb, Austin Burta, and Armand M. Leroi, _Evolution of music by public choice\n_\nJohn Biles, GenJam: A Genetic Algorithm for Generating Jazz Solos (1994)\n\n\nAbstract\nThis paper describes GenJam, a genetic algorithm-based model of a novice jazz musician learning to improvise.\nGenJam maintains hierarchically related populations of melodic ideas that are mapped to specific notes through scales suggested by the chord progression being played.\nAs GenJam plays its solos over the accompaniment of a standard rhythm section, a human mentor gives real-time feedback, which is used to derive fitness values for the individual measures and phrases. GenJam then applies various genetic operators to the populations to breed improved generations of ideas. \n1 Introduction As with most problem-solving activities, musical tasks like composition, arranging and improvising involve a great deal of search. Composers search for the right chords to fit a melody or the right melody to fit a chord progression\n\n\uff08 \u305d\u306e\u4ed6 \u8ad6\u6587 \uff09\n\n\u30b8\u30e7\u30eb\u30c0\u30f3\u30fb\u30a2\u30eb\u30ce\u3001\u8352\u6728 \u5065\u6cbb \u300c\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f\u5e30\u7d0d\u7684\u5b66\u7fd2\u306b\u3088\u308b\u97f3\u58f0\u5bfe\u8a71\u51e6\u7406\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0GA-ILSD\u306b\u304a\u3051\u308b\u8cea\u554f\u5fdc\u7b54\u80fd\u529b\u306b\u3064\u3044\u3066\u300d\n\u5c71\u5ddd \u671b \uff08\u540c\u5fd7\u793e\u5927\u5b66\u5de5\u5b66\u90e8\u77e5\u8b58\u5de5\u5b66\u79d1\uff09\u300c\u5bfe\u8a71\u578b\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3092\u5229\u7528\u3057\u305f\n\u30e6\u30fc\u30b6\u306e\u55dc\u597d\u62bd\u51fa\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0\u306e\u69cb\u7bc9\u300d2006\u5e743\u6708\n\u6589\u85e4 \u512a\u7406, \u5c0f\u8218 \u4eae\u4e4b, \u4f0a\u85e4 \u8cb4\u4e4b \u300c\u5bfe\u8a71\u578b\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f \u30e6\u30fc\u30b6\u306e\u76ee\u7684\u306b\u5408\u3063\u305f\u697d\u66f2\u63a8\u85a6\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0(O)\u300dDEIM Forum 2010\n\n\n\u3053\u3053\u3067\u3001IEC\uff08\u5bfe\u8a71\u578b\u9032\u5316\u8a08\u7b97\uff09 \u3092 \u7528\u3044\u305f \u8cea\u554f\u5fdc\u7b54\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0 \u306e 2002\n\n\n\u5de5\u5b66\u7684\u5074\u9762\u304b\u3089 GA \u3068\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u878d\u5408\u306b\u95a2\u3059\u308b\u7814\u7a76\u304c\u306a\u3055\u308c\u3066\u304d\u305f\u304c,\u5b66\u7fd2\u671f\u9593\u4e2d \u306b\u6559\u5e2b\u4fe1\u53f7\u306b\u5909\u5316\u304c\u53ca\u3076,\u201c\u52d5\u7684\u6027\u8cea\u201d \u3092\u6301\u3064\u5b9f\u9a13\u74b0\u5883\u4e0a\u3067\u306e\u8b70\u8ad6\u304c\u4e4f\u3057\u3044\u306e\u304c\u73fe\u72b6\u3067\u3042\u3063\u305f.\n\u305d\u3053\u3067\u672c\u8ad6\u6587\u3067\u306f , \u81ea \u7136 \u754c \u306e \u751f \u7269 \u304c \u9032 \u5316 \u3068 \u5b66 \u7fd2 \u306b \u3088 \u3063 \u3066 \u69d8 \u3005\u306b \u5909 \u5316 \u3059 \u308b \u74b0 \u5883 \u306b \u9069 \u5fdc \u3059 \u308b \u904e \u7a0b \u3092 \u6a21 \u5023\u3057 \u305f , \u9032 \u5316\u8ad6\u306b\u57fa\u3065\u304f\u69cb\u9020\u9069\u5fdc\u5b66\u7fd2\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4 \u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3092\u63d0\u6848\u3059\u308b.\n\u63d0\u6848\u3059\u308b\u624b\u6cd5\u306f,\u5b66\u7fd2\u4e2d\u306b\u6559\u5e2b\u4fe1\u53f7\u306b\u5909\u5316\u304c\u53ca \u3093\u3060\u5834\u5408\u3067\u3082,\u5b66\u7fd2\u3092\u521d\u671f\u72b6\u614b\u304b\u3089\u884c\u3046\u306e\u3067\u306f\u306a\u304f,\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u69cb\u9020\u3084\u7d50\u5408\u8377\u91cd\u30d9\u30af\u30c8\u30eb,\u5b66\u7fd2\u30d1 \u30e9 \u30e1 \u30fc \u30bf \u5024 \u306e \u7d99 \u627f \u3092 \u8003 \u616e \u3059 \u308b \u9069 \u5fdc \u7684 \u306a \u5b66 \u7fd2 \u3092 \u53ef \u80fd \u3068 \u3059 \u308b \u3082 \u306e \u3067 \u3042 \u308b . \u63d0 \u6848\u3057 \u305f \u624b \u6cd5 \u306e \u6709 \u52b9 \u6027 \u3092 \u691c \u8a3c \u3059 \u308b\u305f\u3081\u306b,1 \u5909\u6570\u95a2\u6570\u306e\u540c\u5b9a\u304a\u3088\u3073 10 bits \u554f\u984c\u306b\u9069\u7528\u3057\u305f\u7d50\u679c\u3092\u3053\u3053\u306b\u5831\u544a\u3059\u308b.\n\n\nKyung-Min Kim1 et.al, Pororobot: A Deep Learning Robot that Plays Video Q&A Games\n\n\nAbstract\n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nHowever, despite these successful results, several key issues still remain to be discussed and improved. In particular, it is essential for an agent to act in a dynamic, uncertain, and asynchronous environment for achieving human-level robot intel- ligence. In this paper, we propose a prototype system for a video Q&A robot \u201cPororobot\u201d. The system uses the state-of-the-art machine learning methods such as a deep concept hierarchy mod- el. In our scenario, a robot and a child plays a video Q&A game together under real world environments. Here we demonstrate preliminary results of the proposed system and discuss some di- rections as future works.\nIntroduction\n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nHowever, in order to interact with a human in an effective manner, a robot agent must deal with real-world environ- ments including dynamic, uncertain, and asynchronous properties based on lifelong learning (Zhang 2013). \nIn this paper, we propose a prototype system using state-of-the-art deep learning methods for a child-robot interaction scenar- io.\nThe deep concept hierarchy (Ha et al. 2015) is used as a knowledge base and deep learning methods including deep convolutional neural networks (CNNs) (Krizhevsky et al. 2012) and recurrent neural networks (RNNs) (Mikolov et al. 2013; Gao et al. 2015) are used for representing features of the video data and generate answers from the questions.\nThe scenario is based on a video Q&A game under the real world environment where a child and a robot asks questions on the cartoon video contents and answers these questions to each other. As a robot platform, we use the Nao Evolution V5. \uff08Diploma Thesis) Neuroevolution for Robot Control, Test Framework and Experimental Evaluation, Institut f\u00a8ur Informatik Lehrstuhl f\u00a8ur Programmierung und Softwaretechnik LUDWIG\u2013MAXIMILIANS\u2013UNIVERSITAT M \u00a8 UNCHEN\n\n\uff08 \u4ee5\u4e0b\u3001\u4e0a\u8a18\u8ad6\u6587\u3088\u308a \u4e00\u90e8 \u629c\u7c8b\u3057\u3066\u8ee2\u8f09 \uff09\n\n\uff08 \u6c34\u4e2d\u30c9\u30ed\u30fc\u30f3\u5236\u5fa1 \uff09\n\nMiguel Duarte, Sancho Moura Oliveira and Anders Lyhne Christensen, Hybrid Control for Large Swarms of Aquatic Drones\n\n\nAbstract\n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nIn this paper, we propose a scalable robotics system based on swarms of small and inexpensive aquatic drones.\nWe take advantage of bio-inspired artificial evolution techniques in order to synthesize scalable and robust collective behaviors for the drones. \nThe behaviors are then combined hierarchically with preprogrammed control in an engineeredcentric approach, allowing the overall behavior for a particular mission to be quickly configured and tested in simulation before the aquatic drones are deployed. \nWe demonstrate the scalability of our hybrid approach by successfully deploying up to 1,000 simulated drones to patrol a 20 km long strip for 24 hours.\n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nBackground\n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nER has been used as an alternative to manual programming of decentralized robotic control, since it allows for the automatic synthesis of control and for the self-organization\nof behavior.\nAn evolutionary algorithm (Goldberg, 1989) optimizes a controller, which is copied to every robot in\nthe system.\nThe algorithm fine-tunes the microscopic rules guiding the individual robots based on the resulting macroscopic behavior, and thus removes the need for manual specification of low-level control (Floreano and Keller, 2010).\nArtificial neural networks (ANN) are widely (but not exclusively) used in ER as robotic controllers. ANNs provide evolution with a relatively smooth search space (Nolfi and Floreano, 2000), are able to represent general and adaptive solutions (Floreano and Mondada, 1994), and are able to tolerate noise, which is inherent to many real-world sensors and actuators (Kam-Chuen et al., 1996).\nIn the domain of multirobot systems, evolutionary techniques have been used in a variety of contexts, from robotic soccer (Uchibe and Asada, 2006), to collective transport (Gro\u00df and Dorigo, 2009), and to establish and maintain data links with swarms of flying robots (Hauert et al., 2009).\nNotable examples of projects in the domain of swarms of aquatic robots are CoCoRo (Schmickl et al., 2011), which focuses on synthesis of control for underwater robots, and ASSISIbf (Halloy et al., 2013), which aims to develop communication channels between robots and animals (fish and\nhoneybees, in particular). \n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nSimulation and Experimental Setup\nWe use JBotEvolver (Duarte et al., 2014c), an open-source, multirobot simulation platform, and neuroevolution framework, for evolution of behavioral control.\nEach neuralnetwork-based controller in our experiments was evolved using a simple generational evolutionary algorithm with parameter values that have led to the synthesis of good solutions in previous studies (Duarte et al., 2014b).\nWe use a population of 100 genomes, and the fitness score assigned to each genome is the mean score obtained in 10 simulations with different initial conditions. \nThe five highest scoring genomes are copied directly to the next generation. \nAnother 19 copies of each genome are made and mutation is applied to each gene with a probability of 10%.\n\n\uff08 \u30ed\u30dc\u30fb\u30c8\u30ec\u30fc\u30c7\u30a3\u30f3\u30b0 / Beberg\u306b\u3088\u308a\u958b\u767a\u3055\u308c\u305f\u3002Beberg\u306f\u4e26\u5217\u30d7\u30ed\u30b8\u30a7\u30af\u30c8\u300cDistributed.net\u300d\u306e\u5275\u8a2d\u8005\u3067\u3001\u3053\u306e\u6280\u8853\u306f\u5f8c\u306b\u3001\u5730\u7403\u5916\u751f\u547d\u4f53\u63a2\u67fb\u7814\u7a76\u300cSeti@Home\u300d\u3067\u5229\u7528\u3055\u308c\u305f\u3002\n\uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\nDeep Learning\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\nAI\u30c8\u30ec\u30fc\u30c7\u30a3\u30f3\u30b0\u306e\u4ee3\u8868\u7684\u306a\u624b\u6cd5\u306fDeep Learning\u306f\u5199\u771f\u3084\u6587\u7ae0\u304b\u3089\u7279\u5b9a\u306e\u30d1\u30bf\u30fc\u30f3\u3092\u691c\u51fa\u3059\u308b\u80fd\u529b\u304c\u7a81\u51fa\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n\u30c4\u30a4\u30fc\u30c8\u304b\u3089\u682a\u4fa1\u306b\u5f71\u97ff\u3059\u308b\u7279\u5b9a\u306e\u4e8b\u8c61\u3092\u691c\u51fa\u3057\u3001\u305d\u308c\u3092\u3082\u3068\u306b\u3001\u6295\u8cc7\u5224\u65ad\u3092\u5b9f\u884c\u3059\u308b\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0\u304c\u958b\u767a\u3055\u308c\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n\u3057\u304b\u3057\u3001Deep Learning\u306e\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u306f\u30b3\u30e2\u30c7\u30a3\u30c6\u30a3\u30fc\u306b\u306a\u308a\u3001\u591a\u304f\u306e\u6295\u8cc7\u5bb6\u304c\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u3092\u63a1\u7528\u3057\u3001\u5dee\u5225\u5316\u304c\u96e3\u3057\u304f\u306a\u3063\u3066\u304d\u305f\u3068\u3082\u3044\u308f\u308c\u308b\u3002\n\u3053\u308c\u306b\u5bfe\u3057\u3066Sentient\u306f\u3001Deep Learning\u306e\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf\u30fc\u3092\u6700\u9069\u5316\u3059\u308b\u3060\u3051\u3067\u306a\u304f\u3001\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u30fb\u30a2\u30fc\u30ad\u30c6\u30af\u30c1\u30e3\u30fc\u81ea\u4f53\u3092\u3082\u6700\u9069\u5316\u3059\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3092\u76ee\u6307\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306b\u3082\u524d\u8ff0\u306eEvolutional Computation\u3092\u5fdc\u7528\u3059\u308b\u3002\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306f\u4e00\u822c\u306b\u300cNeuroevolution\u300d\u3068\u547c\u3070\u308c\u3001\u6a5f\u68b0\u5b66\u7fd2\u306e\u4e00\u624b\u6cd5\u3067\u3001\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u3092\u9032\u5316\u3055\u305b\u308b\u3002\n\u751f\u7269\u304c\u751f\u6210\u3001\u5909\u7570\u3001\u9078\u629e\u3092\u7e70\u308a\u8fd4\u3057\u9032\u5316\u3059\u308b\u3088\u3046\u306b\u3001\u30a2\u30fc\u30ad\u30c6\u30af\u30c1\u30e3\u30fc\u3082\u554f\u984c\u306b\u5bfe\u3057\u3066\u9032\u5316\u3059\u308b\u3002\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306f\u307e\u3060\u958b\u767a\u4e2d\u3067\u3001\u305d\u306e\u6210\u679c\u304c\u6ce8\u76ee\u3055\u308c\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n\n\nWIRED \uff08 Cade Metz \uff09  Business, Date of Publication: 01.25.16, The Rise of the Artificially Intelligent Hedge Fund\n\n\nFor Hodjat, however, the task is to improve on today\u2019s deep learning. \nAnd this may involve combining the technology with evolutionary computation.\nAs he explains it, you could use evolutionary computation to build better deep learning algorithms. This is called neuroevolution.\n\u201cYou can evolve the weights that operate on the deep learner,\u201d Hodjat says.\n\u201cBut you can also evolve the architecture of the deep learner itself.\u201d Microsoft and other outfits are already building deep learning systems through a kind of natural selection, though they may not be using evolutionary computation perse.\n\n\nDan Hu, Algorithmic Currency Trading using NEAT - based Evolutionary\nComputation, May 9, 2014\n\n\nThis paper introduces NEAT-based Evolutionary Computation as the basis for a fully automated trading system application.\nThe system is designed to trade FX markets by detecting protable currency\ncycles in the most widely traded currencies and forecasting future exchange rates.\nTo do this, it relies on a tness function that measures protability, as well as a tness function that measures accuracy of future predictions.\nThe trading system is able to generate consistent gains based on this back-tested and predictive approach.\n\n\n\uff08\u5b66\u58eb\u8ad6\u6587\uff09CARL SANDSTR\u00d6M An evolutionary approach to time series forecasting with artificial neural networks, DEGREE PROJECT, IN COMPUTER SCIENCE , FIRST LEVEL STOCKHOLM, SWEDEN 2015\n\n\nstock market is tested and compared with backpropagation.\nAn neuroevolutionary algorithm is implemented and backtested measuring returns and the normalized-meansquare-error for each algorithm on selected stocks from NASDAQ.\nThe results are not entirely conclusive and further investigation\nwould be needed to say definitely, but it seems as a neuroevolutionary approach could outperform backpropagation for time series prediction. \n\n\nAntonia Azzini, C\u00b6elia da Costa Pereira, and Andrea G.B. Tettamanzi\uff08Universit\u00b5a degli Studi di Milano\uff09Predicting Turning Points in Financial Markets with Fuzzy-Evolutionary and Neuro-Evolutionary Modeling\n\n\nAbstract\nTwo independent evolutionary modeling methods, based on\nfuzzy logic and neural networks respectively, are applied to predicting\ntrend reversals in \u00afnancial time series, and their performances are com-\npared.\nBoth methods are found to give essentially the same results, in-\ndicating that trend reversals are partially predictable.\n\n\uff08 \u4ee5\u4e0b\u3001\u4e0a\u8a18\u8ad6\u6587\u3088\u308a \u4e00\u90e8 \u629c\u7c8b\u3057\u3066\u8ee2\u8f09 \uff09\n\n\nGene I. \u56fd\u9632\u30fb\u56fd\u5bb6\u5b89\u5168\u4fdd\u969c \uff09\n\nBoyles, Brian David, Evolving scout agents for military simulations\n\n\nSimulations play an increasingly significant role in training and preparing the military, particularly in environments with constrained budgets.\nUnfortunately, in most cases a small number of people must control a large number of simulated vehicles and soldiers. \nThis often leads to micromanagement of computer-controlled forces in order to get them to exhibit the human-like characteristics of an enemy force. >\nThis thesis uses Neuroevolution of Augmenting Topologies (NEAT) to train neural networks to perform the role of scouts which analyze the terrain and decide where to place themselves to best observe the enemy forces.\nThe main attribute that the scout agents consider is a vapor flow rate from the enemy starting location to their intended objective, which according to previous studies indicates likely chokepoints along the enemy route. \n*This thesis experiments with different configurations of sensors and fitness functions in order to maximize how much of the enemy team is spotted over the course of the scenario. *\nThe results show that these agents perform better than randomly placed scouts and better than scouts deployed using heuristics in many situations, although not consistently so.\n{{Evolutionary optimization of scout agents using vapor flow is thus a promising approach for developing autonomous scout agents in military simulations**\n\n\uff08 \u5f37\u5316\u5b66\u7fd2\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f\u81ea\u5f8b\u79fb\u52d5\u30ed\u30dc\u30c3\u30c8\u306e\u884c\u52d5\u7372\u5f97\u306b\u95a2\u3059\u308b\u7814\u7a76\u300d\n\u67f4\u7530 \u4fe1\u96c4 \u4e09\u91cd\u5927\u5b66\u5927\u5b66\u9662\u5de5\u5b66\u7814\u7a76\u79d1\u96fb\u6c17\u96fb\u5b50\u5de5\u5b66\u5c02\u653b\nTlauncher111\u3055\u3093 Qiita\u8a18\u4e8b\uff082016/05/14\uff09\u300c\u4eba\u5de5\u77e5\u80fd\u3092\u4f5c\u308b\u4eba\u5de5\u77e5\u80fd\u306e\u7b2c\u4e00\u6b69\u3092\u30b3\u30fc\u30c7\u30a3\u30f3\u30b0\u3057\u305f(\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u3092\u81ea\u52d5\u7684\u306b\u9032\u5316\u3055\u305b\u308b\u65b9\u6cd5)\u300d\n\n\n\n\u3010 \u9644\u8ad6 \u3011\n\n\n\u51fa\u81ea \u306f \u7570\u306a\u308b \u3082\u306e\u306e \u4f3c\u305f\u30a2\u30d7\u30ed\u30fc\u30c1 \u3068\u3057\u3066\u3001GMDH \u3068\u3044\u3046\u3082\u306e \u3082 \u3042\u308b\u3088\u3046\u3060\u3002\n\n\nMiroslav \u0160norek, Pavel Kord\u00edk, Inductive Modelling World Wide the State of the Art\n\n\n3 Connection to neural networks and genetic algorithms\nNeural networks are closely connected to the inductive modelling, although they have different background. \nThe GMDH evolved from the mathematical description of a system by means of Kolmogorov-Gabor polynomial [12].\nNeural networks were at the beginning biologically oriented. \nLater, powerful optimization methods for neural networks (Back-Propagation of error) were invented, allowing building multilayered networks of neurons (MLP) capable of solving nonlinear problems.\nIt has been shown [13] that MLPs are equivalent to mathematical description of a system by means of the Koglomorov theorem (although inner functions are very complex and they have almost fractal character).\nIn recent time both neural networks and GMDH algorithms are optimized by genetic algorithms and it is even harder to distinguish the boundary between both theories.\n*Of course, some neural networks are very different from GMDH (recurrent, modular, spiking neural networks, etc.) *[14].\nThe article [15] shows that the problem of two intertwined spirals can be successfully solved by the MultiLayered Perceptron (MLP), where weights are evolved by the Genetic Algorithm.\nNumber of function evaluation is in this case much higher than when using standard BackPropagation, because the information about gradient of error is not utilized in the GA. On the other hand, in some\napplications, Genetic approach gives better results than BackPropagation [16].\nThe Cascade Correlation algorithm [17] is capable of solving extremely difficult problems.\nIt performs optimally on \"spiral\" benchmarking problem (a network consisting of less than 20 neurons is generated). \nAccording to experiments on real-world data performed in [18], the algorithm has difficulties with avoiding premature convergence to complex topological structures.\nThe main advantage of the Cascade Correlation algorithm is also its main disadvantage.\nIt easily solves extremely difficult problems therefore it is likely to overfit. \nThe recent article [19] proposes an improvement of the Cascade Correlation Algorithm [17]. \nThe original algorithm assumes fully connected network.\nEach neuron is connected to all features and all previously built neurons.\nThe improvement called Evolving Cascade Correlation Networks (ECCN)[19] uses techniques from GMDH theory [1] to choose just relevant inputs for each neuron. \nCascade networks evolved by ECCN overfit data less than fully connected cascade networks.\nRecently, very interesting algorithm for designing recurrent neural networks was proposed in [20, 21].\nThe NeuroEvolution Through Augmenting Topologies (NEAT) is designed for solving reinforcement learning tasks [22], but can be applied also to supervised learning problems.\nSimilarly to the GMDH, NEAT networks grow from a minimal structure up to optimal complexity.\nThe topology and also weights of the NEAT networks are evolved using niching genetic algorithm[23].\nThe NEAT is primary designed for reinforcement learning.\nIt can also solve standard supervised problems.\nWe have applied the NEAT to Two intertwined spiral problem [24], but it failed.\nThe reason why NEAT is unable to evolve successful networks solving the spiral problem is probably that a) the chromosome is too big when evolving architecture and weights of network simultaneously, b) niching alone is unable to protect complex structures. \n\n\u4e0a\u8a18\u306e\u8ad6\u6587\u306e\u307b\u304b\u306b\u3001NeuroEvoltuion \u3068 GMDH \u306e \u4e21\u8005 \u306b \u8a00\u53ca\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b\u8ad6\u8003\u3068\u3057\u3066\u3001\u4ee5\u4e0b \u3092 \u898b\u3064\u3051\u307e\u3057\u305f\u3002\n\nAmalia Foka\uff081999\uff09Time Series Prediction Using Evolving Polynomial Neural Networks\nJan Drchal, Artificial Neural Networks, NeuroEvolution = ANN + EA\n\n\uff08 \u4ee5\u4e0b\u3001\u4e0a\u8a18 \u30b9\u30e9\u30a4\u30c9 \u3088\u308a 85\u2013117\nJurgen Schmidhuber, Deep Learning in Neural Networks: An Overview\n\n\n5.3 1965: Deep Networks Based on the Group Method of Data Handling\n\n\n\nGMDH \u306b\u95a2\u3059\u308b \u30aa\u30f3\u30e9\u30a4\u30f3\u60c5\u5831\n\n\n\uff08 Wikipedia \u82f1\u8a9e\u7248 \uff09Group method of data handling \n\n\nGroup method of data handling (GMDH) is a family of inductive algorithms for computer-based mathematical modeling of multi-parametric datasets that features fully automatic structural and parametric optimization of models.\nGMDH is used in such fields as data mining, knowledge discovery, prediction, complex systems modeling, optimization and pattern recognition.\n\n\n\u7530\u6751\u5766\u4e4b\u30fb\u8fd1\u85e4\u6b63 \u300c\u89e3\u8aac \u6700\u8fd1\u306eGMDH\u306e\u65b9\u6cd5\u8ad6\u3068\u5fdc\u7528\u300d\n\u6939 \u6728 \u7fa9 \u4e00, \u5c0f \u897f \u6b63 \u8eac \u300c\u65b0\u3057\u3044\u30c7\u30fc\u30bf\u51e6\u7406\u6cd5(GMDH)\u306e\u7d39\u4ecb\u3068\u305d\u306e\u88fd\u9244\u30d7\u30ed\u30bb\u30b9\u3078\u306e\u5fdc\u7528\u300d \n\u63da \u5b50\u6c5f \u5c11\u306a\u3044\u30c7\u30fc\u30bf\u304b\u3089\u8907\u96d1\u306a(\u975e\u7dda\u5f62)\u7cfb\u3092\u5927\u96d1\u628a\u306b\u540c\u5b9a\u3059\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3092\u76ee\u7684\u3068\u3057\u3066\u304a\u308a, \u4eca\u65e5\u306e\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30fb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u539f\u578b\u3067\u3042\u308b\u30d1\u30fc\u30bb\u30d7\u30c8\u30ed\u30f3\u306e\u8003\u3048\u65b9\u3092\u30d9\u30fc\u30b9\u306b\u958b\u767a\u3057\u305f\u8a08\u7b97\u30e1\u30ab\u30cb \u63d0\u6848\u5f8c\u6570\u5e74\u3092\u7d4c\u3066\u65e5\u672c\u3067\u3082\u7814\u7a76\u304c\u59cb\u3081\u3089\u308c, 1970\u5e74\u4ee3\u306b\u306f\u6570\u591a\u304f\u306e\u7814\u7a76\u8ad6\u6587\u304c\u767a\u8868\u3055\u308c\u305f3)\uff5e5)\u304c, 1980\u5e74\u4ee3\u306b\u5165\u3063\u3066\u305d\u306e\u7814\u7a76\u71b1\u306f\u4e0b\u706b\u306b\u306a\u3063\u305f.\n\n\nGEvoM Modelling Using GMDH-Type Neural Networks\n\n\nBy means of GMDH algorithm a model can be represented as set of neurons in which different pairs of them in each layer are connected through a quadratic polynomial and thus produce new neurons in the next layer. \nSuch representation can be used in modelling to map inputs to outputs. \n\n\nOsman Dag and Ceylan Yozgatligil, GMDH: An R Package for Short Term Forecasting via GMDH-Type Neural Network Algorithms\n\n\nAbstract\nGroup Method of Data Handling (GMDH)-type neural network algorithms are the heuristic self organization method for the modelling of complex systems. \nGMDH algorithms are utilized for a variety of purposes, examples include identification of physical laws, the extrapolation of physical fields, pattern recognition, clustering, the approximation of multidimensional processes, forecasting without models, etc.\nIn this study, the R package GMDH is presented to make short term forecasting through GMDH-type neural network algorithms. \nThe GMDH package has options to use different transfer functions (sigmoid, radial basis, polynomial, and tangent functions) simultaneously or separately. \nData on cancer death rate of Pennsylvania from 1930 to 2000 are used to illustrate the features of the GMDH package. The results based on ARIMA models and exponential smoothing methods are included for comparison.\n\n\n\uff08 ELESVIER \uff09Isa Ebtehaja et.al, GMDH-type neural network approach for modeling the [1]\u3092\u7528\u3044\u3066\u81ea\u52d5\u7684\u306b\u81ea\u5df1\u7d44\u7e54\u5316\u3059\u308b\u6a5f\u80fd\u3092\u5099\u3048\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n\u305d\u3057\u3066\u3001\u30d5\u30a3\u30fc\u30c9\u30d0\u30c3\u30af\u30eb\u30fc\u30d7\u306e\u6570\u3001\u4e2d\u9593\u5c64\u306e\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30ed\u30f3\u306e\u500b\u6570\u3001\u6709\u76ca\u306a\u5165\u529b\u5909\u6570\u3001\u6700\u9069\u306a\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30ed\u30f3\u69cb\u9020\u306a\u3069\u306e\u69cb\u9020\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf\u3092\u3001\u4e88\u6e2c\u8aa4\u5dee\u5e73\u65b9\u548c(PSS)\u3067\u5b9a\u7fa9\u3055\u308c\u305f\u4e88\u6e2c\u8aa4\u5dee\u8a55\u4fa1\u57fa\u6e96\u3092\u6700\u5c0f\u306b\u3059\u308b\u3088\u3046\u306b\u81ea\u5df1\u9078\u629e\u3059\u308b\u3002\n\u3053\u306e\u305f\u3081\u5bfe\u8c61\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0\u306e\u8907\u96d1\u3055\u306b\u6700\u3082\u9069\u3057\u305f\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u69cb\u9020\u3092\u3001\u81ea\u52d5\u7684\u306b\u69cb\u6210\u3067\u304d\u308b\u3002\u767a\u898b\u7684\u81ea\u5df1\u7d44\u7e54\u5316\u306e\u539f\u7406\u306f\u3001\u751f\u7269\u306e\u9032\u5316\u904e\u7a0b\u3092\u30b3\u30f3\u30d4\u30e5\u30fc\u30bf\u5185\u90e8\u3067\u6a21\u64ec\u3059\u308b\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3067\u3042\u308a\u3001\u9032\u5316\u8ad6\u7684\u8a08\u7b97\u6cd5\u306e\u4e00\u7a2e\u3067\u3042\u308b\u3002 \n\n\n\uff08 ELESVIER \uff09R. Madandousta, R. Ghavidela, N. Nariman-zadehb, Evolutionary design of generalized GMDH-type neural network for prediction of concrete compressive strength using UPV\n\n\nAbstract\nThe main purpose of this paper is to predict the insitu compressive strength of concrete by means of non-destructive approach using ultrasonic pulse velocity (UPV) method. \nFor this purpose generalized GMDH-type (group method of data handling) neural network was developed based on various data obtained experimentally. \nEvolutionary algorithms (EAs) are deployed for optimal design of GMDH-type neural networks.\nA set of experimental data for the training and testing the evolved GMDH-type neural network is employed in which ultrasonic pulse velocity (UPV), concrete age, water\u2013cement ratio and fine/coarse aggregate ratio are considered as inputs and concrete compressive strength is regarded as the output variables.\nSensitivity analysis has also been carried out on one of the obtaining models to study the influence of input parameters on model output. \nThe results show that generalized GMDH-type neural network has a great ability as a feasible tool for prediction of the concrete compressive strength.\n\nNeuroEvolution\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb \u301c \u6df1\u5c64\u5b66\u7fd2 \u306e \u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u69cb\u6210 \u3068 \u96a0\u308c\u5c64\u306e\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf \u3092 \u74b0\u5883\u306e\u5909\u5316 \u306b \u9069\u5fdc\u3055\u305b\u306a\u304c\u3089\u3001\u300c\u9032\u5316\u8ad6\u7684\u300d\u306b\u4e16\u4ee3\u3092\u7e70\u308a\u8fd4\u3057\u3066\u3001\u52d5\u7684 \u306b \u4fee\u6b63\u9032\u5316\u3059\u308b\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb\n\n___\n\n###__\uff11. \u4eca\u56de \u898b\u3064\u3051\u305f\u3082\u306e__\n\n#####**_NeuroEvolution_: Evolutionary Artificial Neural Network, \u76f4\u63a5\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\u306f\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u3059\u3079\u3066\u306e\u7d50\u5408\u3068\u30ce\u30fc\u30c9\u3092\u907a\u4f1d\u5b50\u3068\u3057\u3066\u67d3\u8272\u4f53\u306b\u8a18\u8ff0\u3059\u308b\u3002\n>\u5bfe\u7167\u7684\u306b\u9593\u63a5\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\u306f\u305f\u3044\u3066\u3044\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u3092\u69cb\u6210\u3059\u308b\u30eb\u30fc\u30eb\u3092\u8a18\u8ff0\u3059\u308b\u306e\u307f\u3067\u3042\u308b[2][3]\u3002\n\n\n__DQN ( Deep Q-learning ) \u306e\u540d \u3092 \u4e16\u306b\u77e5\u3089\u3057\u3081\u305f Atari \u30b2\u30fc\u30e0 \u3092 \u30d7\u30ec\u30a4\u3055\u305b\u308b\u8ad6\u6587 \u3082\u3042\u308b__\n\n* [Matthew Hausknecht, Joel Lehman, Risto Miikkulainen, and Peter Stone, _A Neuroevolution Approach to General Atari Game Playin_](http://www.cs.utexas.edu/users/pstone/Papers/bib2html-links/TCIAIG13-mhauskn.pdf)\n\n> This article addresses the challenge of learning to play many different video games with little domainspecific knowledge.\n>\n> Specifically, it introduces a neuro-evolution approach to general Atari 2600 game playing.\n>\n> Four neuro-evolution algorithms were paired with three different state representations and evaluated on a set of 61 Atari games.\n>\n> The neuro-evolution agents represent different points along the spectrum of algorithmic sophistication - including **weight evolution on topologically fixed neural networks (Conventional Neuro-evolution)**, **Covariance Matrix Adaptation Evolution Strategy (CMA-ES)**,\n**evolution of network topology and weights (NEAT)**, and **indirect network encoding (HyperNEAT)**.\n>\n> State representations include an object representation of the game screen, the raw pixels of the game screen, and seeded noise (a comparative baseline). \n>\n> **Results indicate that direct-encoding methods work best on compact state representations while indirect-encoding methods (i.e. HyperNEAT) allow scaling to higher-dimensional representations (i.e. the raw game screen).**\n>\n> Previous approaches based on temporaldifference learning had trouble dealing with the large state spaces and sparse reward gradients often found in Atari games.\n>\n> **Neuro-evolution ameliorates these problems and evolved policies achieve state-of-the-art\nresults, even surpassing human high scores on three games.**\n>\n> **These results suggest that neuro-evolution is a promising approach to general video game playing.**\n\n###__Python \u3092 \u306f\u3058\u3081\u3001\u5404\u8a00\u8a9e\u306e\u30e9\u30a4\u30d6\u30e9\u30ea \u304c \u3059\u3067\u306b \u5229\u7528\u53ef\u80fd__\n\n__\uff08 Python \uff09__\n\n\u30a4\u30f3\u30b9\u30c8\u30fc\u30eb\u65b9\u6cd5\n\n* [NEAT-Python Docs \u00bb Welcome to NEAT-Python\u2019s documentation!](http://neat-python.readthedocs.io/en/latest/)\n\n> pip install neat-python\n\n\u307e\u305f\u306f\n\n> git clone https://github.com/CodeReclaimers/neat-python.git\n\n__\uff08 Ruby \uff09__\n\n* [nilmagnum/ruby_neat](https://github.com/nilmagnum/ruby_neat)\n> a ruby implementation of the neat (neuro evolution of augmented topologies) algorithm\n\n__\uff08 Java \uff09__\n\n* [NEAT Java (JNEAT)](http://nn.cs.utexas.edu/?jneat)\n\n> Released 2002\n>\n> The JNEAT package contains Java source code for the NeuroEvolution of >Augmenting Topologies method (see the original NEAT C++ package).\n>\n> It includes a nice GUI (see  screenshots ), and implementations of experiments for XOR and 3-bit parity. \n>\n>For answers to common questions, refer to our  FAQ .\n>\n> JNEAT was written by Ugo Vierucci based on the original C++ package by Kenneth Stanley. \n\n Versions:\n v1.2 6/24/02 vierucci\n\n* [ANJI (Another NEAT Java Implementation)](http://anji.sourceforge.net/)\n\n> __ANJI (Another NEAT Java Implementation)__\n>\n> Built on top of existing OpenSource projects, ANJI is an implementation of NEAT (Neuro-Evolution of Augmenting Topologies), an algorithm for evolving artificial neural networks developed by Kenneth Stanley, working in the Neural Networks Research Group at the University of Texas at Austin.\n\n__\uff08 Erlang \uff09__\n\n* [Gene I. Sher, _Neuroevolution Through Erlang_](https://www.erlang-factory.com/upload/presentations/735/NeuroevolutionThroughErlang.pdf)\n\n* [Sher, Gene I., _Handbook of Neuroevolution Through Erlang_](http://www.springer.com/us/book/9781461444626)\n\n__\uff08 Haskell \uff09__\n\n* [\uff08 GitHub \uff09aartamonau/haskell-neat](https://github.com/aartamonau/haskell-neat)\n\n> NeuroEvolution of Augmenting Topologies in Haskell \n\n* [\uff08 GitHub \uff09thompsonja/Haskell-NEAT](https://github.com/thompsonja/Haskell-NEAT)\n\n> Implementation of the Neuroevolution of Augmenting Topologies Algorithm\n\n* [\uff08 GitHub \uff09raymoo/NEET](https://github.com/raymoo/NEET)\n\n> Neuroevolution of Augmented Topologies (NEAT) -- in Haskell \n\n___\n\n####__RNN ( recurrent neural network \uff09  \u306e \u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u69cb\u6210 \u3068 \u96a0\u308c\u5c64\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf \u306e \u9069\u5fdc\u5024 \u3092 \u5f97\u308b\u624b\u6cd5 \u3082 \u63d0\u6848\u3055\u308c\u3066\u3044\u308b__\n\uff08\u203b\u4f0a\u5ead\u6589\u5fd7\u5148\u751f\u306e\u6559\u79d1\u66f8\u300e\u65b0\u7dcf\u5b66\u7fd2\u3068\u9032\u5316\u8a08\u7b97\u300fOhmsha (2015) \u306b\u3042\u308b\u3088\u3046\u306b\u3001\u9032\u5316\u8a08\u7b97\u306b\u3088\u3063\u3066\u7372\u5f97\u3067\u304d\u308b\u306e\u306f\u300c\u6700\u9069\u5024\u300d\uff08\u6700\u9069\u5316\u554f\u984c\u306e\u89e3\uff09\u3067\u306f\u306a\u304f\u3001\u300c\u74b0\u5883\u306b\u304a\u3051\u308b\u751f\u5b58\uff08\u8a55\u4fa1\u3001\u5831\u916c\uff09\u3092\u9ad8\u3081\u308b\u300d\u3068\u3044\u3046\u8a55\u4fa1\u8ef8\u3067\u6349\u3048\u305f\u3001\u300c\u74b0\u5883\u300d\u306b\u6700\u3082\u300c\u9069\u5fdc\u300d\u3057\u305f\u81ea\u5df1\u306e\u632f\u308b\u821e\u3044\u306e\u72b6\u614b \u3092 \u5b9f\u73fe\u3059\u308b\uff08\u30a8\u30fc\u30b8\u30a7\u30f3\u30c8\u884c\u52d5\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb\uff09 \u300c\u6700\u9069\u5fdc\uff08\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf\uff09\u5024\u300d\u3067\u3042\u308b\uff09 \n\n* [Peter J. Angeline, Gregory M. Saunders and Jordan B. Pollack, _An Evolutionary Algorithm that Constructs\nRecurrent Neural Networks_](http://demo.cs.brandeis.edu/papers/ieeenn.pdf)\n\n>__Abstract__\n>\n> Standard methods for inducing both the structure and weight values of recurrent neural networks fit an assumed class of architectures to every task. >\n>\n> This simplification is necessary because the interactions between network structure and function are not well understood.\n>\n> Evolutionary computation, which includes genetic algorithms and evolutionary programming, is a population-based search method that has shown promise in such complex tasks.\n>\n> This paper argues that genetic algorithms are inappropriate for network acquisition and describes an evolutionary program, called **GNARL**, that **simultaneously acquires both the structure and weights for recurrent networks**.\n>\n> This algorithm\u2019s empirical acquisition method allows for the emergence of complex behaviors and topologies that are potentially excluded by the artificial architectural constraints imposed in standard network induction methods.\n\n####__NeuroEvolution \u3092 \u63a1\u7528\u3059\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3067\u3001\u904a\u3079\u3070\u904a\u3076\u307b\u3069\u30b2\u30fc\u30e0\u30ad\u30e3\u30e9\u30af\u30bf\u30fc \u304c \u8ce2\u304f\u632f\u308b\u821e\u3046\u3088\u3046\u306b\u306a\u308b \u30c6\u30ec\u30d3\u30b2\u30fc\u30e0 \u306e \u5b9f\u88c5\u3092 \u63d0\u6848\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b \u8ad6\u6587__\n\n* [Kenneth O. Stanley, Bobby D. Bryant and Risto Miikkulainen, _Real-Time Neuroevolution in the NERO Video Game_](http://nn.cs.utexas.edu/downloads/papers/stanley.ieeetec05.pdf)\n\n\uff08 \u3067\u306f\u3001\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u306b\u304a\u3051\u308b\u8a55\u4fa1\u95a2\u6570 \u3092 \u3092\u5b9f\u88c5\u3057\u305f\u5177\u4f53\u4f8b\u3068\u3057\u3066\u3001\u300cMIDI\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f\u30b8\u30e3\u30ba\u306e\u5373\u8208\u6f14\u594f\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0\u30fbGenJam\u300d\u3092\u53d6\u308a\u4e0a\u3052\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n\n> GenJam\u306f\u3001\u3042\u3089\u304b\u3058\u3081\u5165\u529b\u3057\u305f\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u30b7\u30a7\u30af\u30b7\u30e7\u30f3\u3068\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u9032\u884c\u306b\u6cbf\u3063\u3066\u3001\u96c6\u56e3\u306e\u500b\u4f53\u3092\u7d44\u307f\u5408\u308f\u305b\u3066\u30e1\u30ed\u30c7\u30a3\u3068\u3057\u3066\u6f14\u594f\u3057\u307e\u3059\u3002\n>\n> \u305d\u308c\u3092\u805e\u3044\u305f\u8a55\u4fa1\u8005\u306f\u3001\u3088\u3044\u3068\u601d\u3063\u305f\u77ac\u9593\u306b\"g\"\uff08good\uff09\u3001\u60aa\u3051\u308c\u3070\"b\"(bad\uff09\u3092\u62bc\u3057\u3066\u3001\u305d\u308c\u305e\u308c\u306e\u500b\u4f53\u306b\u8a55\u4fa1\u3092\u4e0e\u3048\u307e\u3059\u3002\n>\n>\u3053\u3046\u3057\u3066\u4e0e\u3048\u3089\u3048\u305f\u8a55\u4fa1\u3092\u3082\u3068\u306b\u4e16\u4ee3\u4ea4\u4ee3\u3092\u91cd\u306d\u3066\u3044\u304f\u3046\u3061\u306b\u3001\u3088\u308a\u3088\u3044\uff08\u5c11\u306a\u304f\u3068\u3082\u8a55\u4fa1\u8005\u306e\u597d\u307f\u306b\u8fd1\u3044\uff09\u5c0f\u7bc0\u30fb\u30d5\u30ec\u30fc\u30ba\u306e\u96c6\u56e3\u304c\u4f5c\u308a\u51fa\u3055\u308c\u307e\u3059\u3002\n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n> GenJam\u306f\u4eba\u9593\u304c\u3042\u307e\u308a\u601d\u3044\u3064\u304b\u306a\u3044\u3088\u3046\u306a\u6f14\u594f\u3092\u8fd4\u3057\u3066\u304f\u308b\u306e\u3067\u3001\u9a5a\u304b\u3055\u308c\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3082\u3057\u3070\u3057\u3070\u3042\u308a\u307e\u3059\u3002\n\n* [Robert M. MacCallum, Matthias Mauchb, Austin Burta, and Armand M. Leroi, _Evolution of music by public choice\n_](http://www.pnas.org/content/109/30/12081.long)\n\n* [John Biles, _GenJam: A Genetic Algorithm for Generating Jazz Solos (1994)_](http://citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/summary?doi=10.1.1.55.6146)\n\n>__Abstract__\n>\n>This paper describes GenJam, a genetic algorithm-based model of a novice jazz musician learning to improvise.\n>\n> GenJam maintains hierarchically related populations of melodic ideas that are mapped to specific notes through scales suggested by the chord progression being played.\n>\n> As GenJam plays its solos over the accompaniment of a standard rhythm section, a human mentor gives real-time feedback, which is used to derive fitness values for the individual measures and phrases. GenJam then applies various genetic operators to the populations to breed improved generations of ideas. \n>\n> 1 Introduction As with most problem-solving activities, musical tasks like composition, arranging and improvising involve a great deal of search. Composers search for the right chords to fit a melody or the right melody to fit a chord progression\n\n\uff08 \u305d\u306e\u4ed6 \u8ad6\u6587 \uff09\n\n* [\u30b8\u30e7\u30eb\u30c0\u30f3\u30fb\u30a2\u30eb\u30ce\u3001\u8352\u6728 \u5065\u6cbb \u30e6\u30fc\u30b6\u306e\u55dc\u597d\u62bd\u51fa\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0\u306e\u69cb\u7bc9\u300d2006\u5e743\u6708](http://mikilab.doshisha.ac.jp/dia/research/pdga/papers/graduate_yamakawa.pdf)\n\n* \u540c\u4e00\u8a71\u8005 \u304c \u597d\u3080 \u56de\u7b54\u306e\u50be\u5411 \u304c \u6642\u9593\u3068\u3068\u3082\u306b\u5909\u5316\u3057\u3066\u3044\u304f\u72b6\u6cc1\n\n___\n\n####__NeuroEvolution\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb \u304c \u4f7f\u3048\u305d\u3046\u3060__\n\n* [\u5927\u679d \u771f\u4e00\u307b\u304b \u300c\u9032\u5316\u8ad6\u306b\u57fa\u3065\u304f\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8 \u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e \u69cb\u9020\u9069\u5fdc\u5b66\u7fd2\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u306e\u69cb\u6210\u300d\u60c5\u5831\u51e6\u7406\u5b66\u4f1a\u8ad6\u6587\u8a8c Vol. 43\nNo. 8 Aug. \u5de5\u5b66\u7684\u5074\u9762\u304b\u3089 GA \u3068\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u878d\u5408\u306b\u95a2\u3059\u308b\u7814\u7a76\u304c\u306a\u3055\u308c\u3066\u304d\u305f\u304c,\u5b66\u7fd2\u671f\u9593\u4e2d \u306b\u6559\u5e2b\u4fe1\u53f7\u306b\u5909\u5316\u304c\u53ca\u3076,\u201c\u52d5\u7684\u6027\u8cea\u201d \u3092\u6301\u3064\u5b9f\u9a13\u74b0\u5883\u4e0a\u3067\u306e\u8b70\u8ad6\u304c\u4e4f\u3057\u3044\u306e\u304c\u73fe\u72b6\u3067\u3042\u3063\u305f.\n>\n> \u305d\u3053\u3067\u672c\u8ad6\u6587\u3067\u306f , \u81ea \u7136 \u754c \u306e \u751f \u7269 \u304c \u9032 \u5316 \u3068 \u5b66 \u7fd2 \u306b \u3088 \u3063 \u3066 \u69d8 \u3005\u306b \u5909 \u5316 \u3059 \u308b \u74b0 \u5883 \u306b \u9069 \u5fdc \u3059 \u308b \u904e \u7a0b \u3092 \u6a21 \u5023\u3057 \u305f , \u9032 \u5316\u8ad6\u306b\u57fa\u3065\u304f\u69cb\u9020\u9069\u5fdc\u5b66\u7fd2\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4 \u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3092\u63d0\u6848\u3059\u308b.\n>\n> \u63d0\u6848\u3059\u308b\u624b\u6cd5\u306f,\u5b66\u7fd2\u4e2d\u306b\u6559\u5e2b\u4fe1\u53f7\u306b\u5909\u5316\u304c\u53ca \u3093\u3060\u5834\u5408\u3067\u3082,\u5b66\u7fd2\u3092\u521d\u671f\u72b6\u614b\u304b\u3089\u884c\u3046\u306e\u3067\u306f\u306a\u304f,\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u69cb\u9020\u3084\u7d50\u5408\u8377\u91cd\u30d9\u30af\u30c8\u30eb,\u5b66\u7fd2\u30d1 \u30e9 \u30e1 \u30fc \u30bf \u5024 \u306e \u7d99 \u627f \u3092 \u8003 \u616e \u3059 \u308b \u9069 \u5fdc \u7684 \u306a \u5b66 \u7fd2 \u3092 \u53ef \u80fd \u3068 \u3059 \u308b \u3082 \u306e \u3067 \u3042 \u308b . \u63d0 \u6848\u3057 \u305f \u624b \u6cd5 \u306e \u6709 \u52b9 \u6027 \u3092 \u691c \u8a3c \u3059 \u308b\u305f\u3081\u306b,1 \u5909\u6570\u95a2\u6570\u306e\u540c\u5b9a\u304a\u3088\u3073 10 bits \u554f\u984c\u306b\u9069\u7528\u3057\u305f\u7d50\u679c\u3092\u3053\u3053\u306b\u5831\u544a\u3059\u308b.\n\n* [Kyung-Min Kim1 _et.al, Pororobot: A Deep Learning Robot that Plays Video Q&A Games_](http://www.aaai.org/ocs/index.php/FSS/FSS15/paper/view/11670/11533)\n\n>__Abstract__\n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n>However, despite these successful results, several key issues still remain to be discussed and improved. In particular, it is essential for an agent to act in a dynamic, uncertain, and asynchronous environment for achieving human-level robot intel- ligence. In this paper, we propose a prototype system for a video Q&A robot \u201cPororobot\u201d. The system uses the state-of-the-art machine learning methods such as a deep concept hierarchy mod- el. In our scenario, a robot and a child plays a video Q&A game together under real world environments. Here we demonstrate preliminary results of the proposed system and discuss some di- rections as future works.\n>\n\n>__Introduction__\n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n>However, in order to interact with a human in an effective manner, __a robot agent must deal with real-world environ- ments including dynamic, uncertain, and asynchronous properties based on lifelong learning__ (Zhang 2013). \n>\n> In this paper, we propose a prototype system using state-of-the-art deep learning methods for a child-robot interaction scenar- io.\n>\n> The deep concept hierarchy (Ha et al. 2015) is used as a knowledge base and deep learning methods including deep convolutional neural networks (CNNs) (Krizhevsky et al. 2012) and recurrent neural networks (RNNs) (Mikolov et al. 2013; Gao et al. 2015) are used for representing features of the video data and generate answers from the questions.\n>\n> The scenario is based on a video Q&A game under the real world environment where a child and a robot asks questions on the cartoon video contents and answers these questions to each other. As a robot platform, we use the Nao Evolution V5. \n>\n\n\u4ee5\u4e0b\u306f\u3001NeuroEvolution\u3068\u306f\u30a2\u30d7\u30ed\u30fc\u30c1\u304c\u9055\u3046\u304b\u3082\u3057\u308c\u306a\u3044\u304c\u3001\u95a2\u9023\u4e8b\u4f8b\u3068\u3057\u3066\u63b2\u8f09\u3002\n\n* \u300c\u52d5\u7684\u518d\u7de8\u6210\u6a5f\u80fd\u3092\u6709\u3059\u308b\u795e\u7d4c\u56de\u8def\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f\u6b69\u5bb9\u5236\u5fa1\u300d\u96fb \u5b66 \u8ad6C,119\u5dfb12\u53f7,\u5e73\u621011\u5e74](https://www.jstage.jst.go.jp/article/ieejeiss1987/119/12/119_12_1567/_pdf)\n\n>\u8fd1\u5e74,\u30ed \u30dc \u30c3\u30c8\u306e \u30b3\u30f3 \u30c8\u30ed\u30fc \u30e9\u3092\u9032\u5316\u7684\u8a08\u7b97\u624b\u6cd5 \u3092\u7528 \u3044\u3066 \u81ea\u5f8b \u7684\u306b\u69cb \u7bc9\u3059\u308b\u9032 \u5316\u30ed\u30dc\u30c6 \u30a3\u30af\u30b9(Ev01utionary RobotiCS,\u4ee5 \u4e0bER\u3068 \u7565\u3059)\u306e \u7814\u7a76\u304c\u6ce8\u76ee\u3092\u96c6\u3081\u3064\u3064\u3042\u308b\u3002\n>\n> \u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306f,\u3053\u308c\u307e\u3067\u3042\u308b\u56fa\u5b9a\u69cb\u9020\u306e\u4e0b\u3067 \u9069\u5207\u306a\u30b7\u30ca\u30d7\u30b9\u8377\u91cd\u3092\u554f\u984c\u306b\u5408\u308f\u305b\u3066\u8abf\u6574\u3059\u308b\u3068\u3044\u3046\u65b9\u6cd5 \u304c\u53d6\u3089\u308c\u3066\u304d\u305f\u3002\n>\n>\u3057\u304b\u3057\u306a\u304c\u3089,\u5b9f\u969b\u306e\u795e\u7d4c\u7cfb\u3067\u306f\u6c7a\u3057\u3066\u56fa \u5b9a \u3055\u308c\u305f\u795e\u7d4c\u56de\u8def\u306b\u57fa\u3065 \u304d\u60c5\u5831\u51e6\u7406\u3092\u884c \u3063\u3066\u3044\u308b\u306e\u3067\u306f\u306a \u672c\u30b7\u30b9\u30c6\u30e0\u306b\u304a\u3044\u3066\u306f,\u30ed \u30dc \u30c3\u30c8\u306e\u30bb\u30f3\u30b5\u5165\u529b\u304b \u3068,\u62e1\u6563 \u3055\u308c\u305fNM \u306e\u30b7\u30ca\u30d7\u30b9\u7d50\u5408\u3078\u306e\u5f71\u97ff \u3068\u3044 \u3046,\u30b5 \u30a4\u30af\u30ea\u30c3\u30af\u306a\u76f8\u4e92\u4f5c\u7528 \u306b\u3088\u308b\u52d5\u7684\u518d\u7de8\u6210\u904e\u7a0b\u3092\u7d4c\u3066,\u305d\u306e\u72b6\u6cc1\u306b\u304a\u3051\u308b\u795e\u7d4c\u56de\u8def\u304c \u767a\u73fe\u3059\u308b(\u56f3 \u308c\u305f\u7d50\u7dda\u3092\u793a\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002\n>\n> \u307e\u305f,\u7d50\u7dda\u306e\u6fc3\u6de1\u306f\u3053\u306e\u72b6\u6cc1\u4e0b\u3067\u30b7\u30ca\u30d7\u30b9\u8377\u91cd\u304c\u5f37\u5316/\u5f31 \u5316\u3055 \u304c\u4e3b\u6d41\u3068\u306a\u3063\u3066\u304d\u305f.\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30ed\u30a8\u30dc\u30ea\u30e5\u30fc\u30b7\u30e7\u30f3\u306b\u3088\u308b\u4eba \u304c\u907a\u4f1d\u5b50\u306b\u30b3\u30fc\u30c9\u5316\u3055\u308c\u4e00\u500b\u4f53\u3092\u5f62\u6210\u3059\u308b.\u305d\u306e ANN \u3092 \u7528\u3044\u3066\u3042\u308b\u6642\u70b9\u306b\u304a\u3051\u308b\u300c\u74b0\u5883\u5165\u529b\u304b\u3089\u884c\u52d5\u51fa\u529b\u300d\u3092\u6c7a\u5b9a \u904e\u7a0b\u3092\u3042\u308b\u30b9\u30c6\u30c3\u30d7\u6570\u7e70\u308a\u8fd4\u3057\u305f\u7d50\u679c\u304b\u3089\u500b\u4f53\u306e\u8a55\u4fa1\u3092\u884c \u3046.\u305f\u3068\u3048\u3070,\u4eba\u5de5\u751f\u7269\u304c\u3088\u308a\u76ee\u7684\u5730\u306b\u8fd1\u3065\u3044\u3066\u3044\u308b\u5834\u5408 \u306b\u57fa\u3065\u3044\u3066\u751f\u6210\u3059\u308b.\u3053\u306e\u3088\u3046\u306a\u904e\u7a0b \u751f\u6210\u3055\u308c\u308b.\u3059\u306a\u308f\u3061,\u8a55\u4fa1\u5024\u3092\u9ad8\u304f\u3059\u308b\u3088\u3046\u306a\u884c\u52d5\u3092\u5b9f \u73fe\u3059\u308b ANN \u30b3\u30f3\u30c8\u30ed\u30fc\u30e9\u304c\u751f\u6210\u3067\u304d\u308b.\n\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30ed\u30a8\u30dc\u30ea\u30e5\u30fc\u30b7\u30e7\u30f3\u306f,ANN \u306e\u7d50\u5408\u91cd\u307f\u3084\u7d50\u5408\u305d \u306e\u3082\u306e\u306e\u69cb\u9020\u3092 GA \u3067\u9032\u5316\u3055\u305b\u308b\u3082\u306e\u3068\u6349\u3048\u3089\u308c\u308b\u304c,\u8fd1 ANN(\u4e0b\u4f4d\u968e\u5c64 ANN) \u3067\u884c\u52d5\u30b3\u30f3\u30c8\u30ed\u30fc\u30e9 _Improving Reinforcement Learning Function Approximators via Neuroevolution_](https://www.aaai.org/Papers/AAAI/2005/DC05-016.pdf)\n\n___\n\n##__\u3010 \u9818\u57df\u5225 \u5b9f\u88c5\u4e8b\u4f8b \u3011__\n\n###__\u975e\u5e38\u306b\u591a\u304f\u306e\u9818\u57df \u3067 NeuroEvolution \u306f\u5404\u7a2e\u6a5f\u5668\u3001\u30b5\u30fc\u30d3\u30b9 \u306b \u3059\u3067\u306b\u5b9f\u88c5\u3055\u308c\u3066\u3044\u308b\u6a21\u69d8\u3002__\n\n__\uff08 \u9854\u8a8d\u8b58 \uff09__\n\n* [Jorge Garc\u00edia Bueno _et.al, Facial gesture recognition using active appearance models based on neural evolution_](http://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?id=2157721)\n\n__\uff08 \u30ed\u30dc\u30c3\u30c8\u5236\u5fa1 \uff09__\n\n* [Michael W\u00a8urtinger \uff08Diploma Thesis) _Neuroevolution for Robot Control, Test Framework and Experimental Evaluation_, Institut f\u00a8ur Informatik Lehrstuhl f\u00a8ur Programmierung und Softwaretechnik LUDWIG\u2013MAXIMILIANS\u2013UNIVERSITAT M \u00a8 UNCHEN](https://www.pst.ifi.lmu.de/Lehre/Abschlussarbeiten/vorlagen/thesis-wuertinger_2011-12-19.pdf)\n\n\uff08 \u4ee5\u4e0b\u3001\u4e0a\u8a18\u8ad6\u6587\u3088\u308a \u4e00\u90e8 \u629c\u7c8b\u3057\u3066\u8ee2\u8f09 \uff09\n\n![pic3.PNG](https://qiita-image-store.s3.amazonaws.com/0/43487/27bc2757-6f62-b9a2-615d-2d507f22464d.png)\n\n\n__\uff08 \u6c34\u4e2d\u30c9\u30ed\u30fc\u30f3\u5236\u5fa1 \uff09__\n\n* [Miguel Duarte, Sancho Moura Oliveira and Anders Lyhne Christensen, _Hybrid Control for Large Swarms of Aquatic Drones_](http://miguelduarte.pt/media/publications/duarte2014alife_aquatic.pdf)\n\n>__Abstract__\n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n>In this paper, we propose a scalable robotics system based on swarms of small and inexpensive aquatic drones.\n>\n> We take advantage of bio-inspired artificial evolution techniques in order to synthesize scalable and robust collective behaviors for the drones. \n>\n> The behaviors are then combined hierarchically with preprogrammed control in an engineeredcentric approach, allowing the overall behavior for a particular mission to be quickly configured and tested in simulation before the aquatic drones are deployed. \n>\n> We demonstrate the scalability of our hybrid approach by successfully deploying up to 1,000 simulated drones to patrol a 20 km long strip for 24 hours.\n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n> __Background__\n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n> ER has been used as an alternative to manual programming of decentralized robotic control, since it allows for the automatic synthesis of control and for the self-organization\nof behavior.\n>\n> An evolutionary algorithm (Goldberg, 1989) optimizes a controller, which is copied to every robot in\nthe system.\n>\n> The algorithm fine-tunes the microscopic rules guiding the individual robots based on the resulting macroscopic behavior, and thus removes the need for manual specification of low-level control (Floreano and Keller, 2010).\n>\n> Artificial neural networks (ANN) are widely (but not exclusively) used in ER as robotic controllers. ANNs provide evolution with a relatively smooth search space (Nolfi and Floreano, 2000), are able to represent general and adaptive solutions (Floreano and Mondada, 1994), and are able to tolerate noise, which is inherent to many real-world sensors and actuators (Kam-Chuen et al., 1996).\n>\n> In the domain of multirobot systems, evolutionary techniques have been used in a variety of contexts, from robotic soccer (Uchibe and Asada, 2006), to collective transport (Gro\u00df and Dorigo, 2009), and to establish and maintain data links with swarms of flying robots (Hauert et al., 2009).\n>\n> Notable examples of projects in the domain of swarms of aquatic robots are CoCoRo (Schmickl et al., 2011), which focuses on synthesis of control for underwater robots, and ASSISIbf (Halloy et al., 2013), which aims to develop communication channels between robots and animals (fish and\nhoneybees, in particular). \n>\n> \uff08 \u4e2d\u7565 \uff09\n>\n>__Simulation and Experimental Setup__\n>\n> We use JBotEvolver (Duarte et al., 2014c), an open-source, multirobot simulation platform, and **neuroevolution framework, for evolution of behavioral control.**\n>\n> Each neuralnetwork-based controller in our experiments was evolved using a simple generational evolutionary algorithm with parameter values that have led to the synthesis of good solutions in previous studies (Duarte et al., 2014b).\n>\n> We use a population of 100 genomes, and the fitness score assigned to each genome is the mean score obtained in 10 simulations with different initial conditions. \n>\n> The five highest scoring genomes are copied directly to the next generation. \n>\n> Another 19 copies of each genome are made and mutation is applied to each gene with a probability of 10%.\n\n__\uff08 **\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306b\u3082\u524d\u8ff0\u306eEvolutional Computation\u3092\u5fdc\u7528\u3059\u308b\u3002\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306f\u4e00\u822c\u306b\u300cNeuroevolution\u300d\u3068\u547c\u3070\u308c\u3001\u6a5f\u68b0\u5b66\u7fd2\u306e\u4e00\u624b\u6cd5\u3067\u3001\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u3092\u9032\u5316\u3055\u305b\u308b\u3002**\n>\n>**\u751f\u7269\u304c\u751f\u6210\u3001\u5909\u7570\u3001\u9078\u629e\u3092\u7e70\u308a\u8fd4\u3057\u9032\u5316\u3059\u308b\u3088\u3046\u306b\u3001\u30a2\u30fc\u30ad\u30c6\u30af\u30c1\u30e3\u30fc\u3082\u554f\u984c\u306b\u5bfe\u3057\u3066\u9032\u5316\u3059\u308b\u3002\u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306f\u307e\u3060\u958b\u767a\u4e2d\u3067\u3001\u305d\u306e\u6210\u679c\u304c\u6ce8\u76ee\u3055\u308c\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3002**\n\n\n* [WIRED \uff08 Cade Metz \uff09\tBusiness, Date of Publication: 01.25.16, _The Rise of the Artificially Intelligent Hedge Fund_](https://www.wired.com/2016/01/the-rise-of-the-artificially-intelligent-hedge-fund/)\n\n> For Hodjat, however, the task is to improve on today\u2019s __deep learning__. \n>\n> __And this may involve combining the technology with evolutionary computation.__\n>\n> As he explains it, __you could use evolutionary computation to build better deep learning algorithms. This is called neuroevolution.__\n>\n> \u201cYou can evolve the weights that operate on the deep learner,\u201d Hodjat says.\n>\n> \u201cBut you can also evolve the architecture of the deep learner itself.\u201d Microsoft and other outfits are already building deep learning systems through a kind of natural selection, though they may not be using evolutionary computation perse.\n\n* [Dan Hu, _Algorithmic Currency Trading using NEAT - based Evolutionary\nComputation_, May 9, 2014](https://www.cs.swarthmore.edu/~meeden/cs81/s14/papers/DanOmar.pdf)\n\n> This paper introduces NEAT-based Evolutionary Computation as the basis for a fully automated trading system application.\n>\n> The system is designed to trade FX markets by detecting pro\ftable currency\ncycles in the most widely traded currencies and forecasting future exchange rates.\n>\n> To do this, it relies on a \ftness function that measures pro\ftability, as well as a \ftness function that measures accuracy of future predictions.\n>\n> The trading system is able to generate consistent gains based on this back-tested and predictive approach.\n\n* [\uff08\u5b66\u58eb\u8ad6\u6587\uff09CARL SANDSTR\u00d6M _An evolutionary approach to time series forecasting with artificial neural networks_, DEGREE PROJECT, IN COMPUTER SCIENCE , FIRST LEVEL STOCKHOLM, SWEDEN 2015](http://www.diva-portal.org/smash/get/diva2:815021/FULLTEXT01.pdf)\n\n> stock market is tested and compared with backpropagation.\n>\n> **An neuroevolutionary algorithm** is implemented and backtested measuring returns and the normalized-meansquare-error for each algorithm on **selected stocks from NASDAQ**.\n>\n> **The results are not entirely conclusive and further investigation\nwould be needed to say definitely, but it seems as a neuroevolutionary approach could outperform backpropagation for time series prediction**. \n\n* [Antonia Azzini, C\u00b6elia da Costa Pereira, and Andrea G.B. Tettamanzi\uff08Universit\u00b5a degli Studi di Milano\uff09_Predicting Turning Points in Financial Markets with Fuzzy-Evolutionary and Neuro-Evolutionary Modeling_](http://www.i3s.unice.fr/~cpereira/EvoFIN2009-final.pdf)\n\n>__Abstract__\n>\n> __Two independent evolutionary modeling methods, based on\nfuzzy logic and neural networks respectively, are applied to predicting\ntrend reversals in \u00afnancial time series__, and their performances are com-\npared.\n>\n> Both methods are found to give essentially the same results, in-\ndicating that trend reversals are partially predictable.\n\n\n\uff08 \u4ee5\u4e0b\u3001\u4e0a\u8a18\u8ad6\u6587\u3088\u308a \u4e00\u90e8 \u629c\u7c8b\u3057\u3066\u8ee2\u8f09 \uff09\n\n![pic2.PNG](https://qiita-image-store.s3.amazonaws.com/0/43487/acedf6d8-8461-a2c9-399f-d6164762468c.png)\n\n\n\n* [Gene I. \u3059\u3067\u306b\u5229\u7528\u3055\u308c\u3066\u3044\u308b\u3068\u307f\u3066\u3001\u5927\u5c40\u3092\u898b\u8aa4\u308b\u3053\u3068\u306f\u306a\u3044\u3060\u308d\u3046\u3002 \n\n__\uff08 \u56fd\u9632\u30fb\u56fd\u5bb6\u5b89\u5168\u4fdd\u969c \uff09__\n\n* [Boyles, Brian David, _Evolving scout agents for military simulations_](https://repositories.lib.utexas.edu/handle/2152/31850)\n\n> Simulations play an increasingly significant role in training and preparing the military, particularly in environments with constrained budgets.\n>\n>  Unfortunately, in most cases a small number of people must control a large number of simulated vehicles and soldiers. \n>\n> This often leads to micromanagement of computer-controlled forces in order to get them to exhibit the human-like characteristics of an enemy force. >\n> \n> **This thesis uses Neuroevolution of Augmenting Topologies (NEAT) to train neural networks to perform the role of scouts which analyze the terrain and decide where to place themselves to best observe the enemy forces.**\n>\n> The main attribute that the scout agents consider is a vapor flow rate from the enemy starting location to their intended objective, which according to previous studies indicates likely chokepoints along the enemy route. \n>\n> **This thesis experiments with different configurations of sensors and fitness functions in order to maximize how much of the enemy team is spotted over the course of the scenario. **\n>\n> **The results show that these agents perform better than randomly placed scouts and better than scouts deployed using heuristics in many situations, although not consistently so.**\n>\n> {{Evolutionary optimization of scout agents using vapor flow is thus a promising approach for developing autonomous scout agents in military simulations**\n\n__\uff08 \u30bd\u30d5\u30c8\u30a6\u30a7\u30a2\u81ea\u52d5\u30c1\u30e5\u30fc\u30cb\u30f3\u30b0 \uff09__\n\n* [\uff08 SlideShare \uff09Takahiro Katagiri [\u67f4\u7530 \u4fe1\u96c4 \uff08\u4fee\u58eb\u8ad6\u6587\uff09\u300c\u4e8c\u91cd\u5b66\u7fd2\u5668\u3092\u7528\u3044\u308b\u5f37\u5316\u5b66\u7fd2\u306e\n [Tlauncher111\u3055\u3093 Qiita\u8a18\u4e8b\uff082016/05/14\uff09\u300c\u4eba\u5de5\u77e5\u80fd\u3092\u4f5c\u308b\u4eba\u5de5\u77e5\u80fd\u306e\u7b2c\u4e00\u6b69\u3092\u30b3\u30fc\u30c7\u30a3\u30f3\u30b0\u3057\u305f(\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u3092\u81ea\u52d5\u7684\u306b\u9032\u5316\u3055\u305b\u308b\u65b9\u6cd5)\u300d](http://qiita.com/Tlauncher111/items/1120c6dbb5ef920d3cd0)\n\n___\n\n#__\u3010 \u9644\u8ad6 \u3011__\n\n##__\u51fa\u81ea \u306f \u7570\u306a\u308b \u3082\u306e\u306e \u4f3c\u305f\u30a2\u30d7\u30ed\u30fc\u30c1 \u3068\u3057\u3066\u3001GMDH \u3068\u3044\u3046\u3082\u306e \u3082 \u3042\u308b\u3088\u3046\u3060\u3002__\n\n* [Miroslav \u0160norek, Pavel Kord\u00edk, _Inductive Modelling World Wide the State of the Art_](http://www.mgua.irtc.org.ua/attach/ICIM-IWIM/2007/42.pdf)\n\n> __3 Connection to neural networks and genetic algorithms__\n>\n> Neural networks are closely connected to the inductive modelling, although they have different background. \n>\n> **The GMDH** evolved **from the mathematical description of a system by means of Kolmogorov-Gabor polynomial** [12].\n>\n> Neural networks were at the beginning biologically oriented. \n>\n> Later, powerful optimization methods for neural networks (Back-Propagation of error) were invented, allowing building multilayered networks of neurons (MLP) capable of solving nonlinear problems.\n>\n> It has been shown [13] that MLPs are equivalent to mathematical description of a system by means of the Koglomorov theorem (although inner functions are very complex and they have almost fractal character).\n>\n> **In recent time both neural networks and GMDH algorithms are optimized by genetic algorithms** and **it is even harder to distinguish the boundary between both theories.**\n>\n> **Of course, some neural networks are very different from GMDH (recurrent, modular, spiking neural networks, etc.) **[14].\n>\n> The article [15] shows that the problem of two intertwined spirals can be successfully solved by the MultiLayered Perceptron (MLP), where weights are evolved by the Genetic Algorithm.\n>\n> Number of function evaluation is in this case much higher than when using standard BackPropagation, because the information about gradient of error is not utilized in the GA. On the other hand, in some\napplications, Genetic approach gives better results than BackPropagation [16].\n>\n> The Cascade Correlation algorithm [17] is capable of solving extremely difficult problems.\n>\n> It performs optimally on \"spiral\" benchmarking problem (a network consisting of less than 20 neurons is generated). \n>\n> According to experiments on real-world data performed in [18], the algorithm has difficulties with avoiding premature convergence to complex topological structures.\n>\n> The main advantage of the Cascade Correlation algorithm is also its main disadvantage.\n>\n> It easily solves extremely difficult problems therefore it is likely to overfit. \n>\n> The recent article [19] proposes an improvement of the Cascade Correlation Algorithm [17]. \n>\n> The original algorithm assumes fully connected network.\n> \n> Each neuron is connected to all features and all previously built neurons.\n>\n>  The improvement called Evolving Cascade Correlation Networks (ECCN)[19] uses techniques from GMDH theory [1] to choose just relevant inputs for each neuron. \n>\n> Cascade networks evolved by ECCN overfit data less than fully connected cascade networks.\n>\n> **Recently, very interesting algorithm for designing recurrent neural networks was proposed in [20, 21].**\n>\n> **The NeuroEvolution Through Augmenting Topologies (NEAT)** is designed **for solving reinforcement learning tasks [22], but can be applied also to supervised learning problems.**\n>\n> **Similarly to the GMDH, NEAT networks grow from a minimal structure up to optimal complexity.**\n>\n> The topology and also weights of the NEAT networks are evolved using niching genetic algorithm[23].\n>\n> **The NEAT is primary designed for reinforcement learning.**\n>\n> It can also solve standard supervised problems.\n>\n> **We have applied the NEAT to Two intertwined spiral problem [24], but it failed.**\n>\n> The reason why NEAT is unable to evolve successful networks solving the spiral problem is probably that a) the chromosome is too big when evolving architecture and weights of network simultaneously, b) niching alone is unable to protect complex structures. \n\n__\u4e0a\u8a18\u306e\u8ad6\u6587\u306e\u307b\u304b\u306b\u3001NeuroEvoltuion \u3068 GMDH \u306e \u4e21\u8005 \u306b \u8a00\u53ca\u3057\u3066\u3044\u308b\u8ad6\u8003\u3068\u3057\u3066\u3001\u4ee5\u4e0b \u3092 \u898b\u3064\u3051\u307e\u3057\u305f\u3002__\n\n* [Amalia Foka\uff081999\uff09_Time Series Prediction Using Evolving Polynomial Neural Networks_](http://citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/download?doi=10.1.1.80.7086&rep=rep1&type=pdf)\n\n* [Jan Drchal, _Artificial Neural Networks, NeuroEvolution = ANN + EA_](https://cw.felk.cvut.cz/w/_media/courses/a4m33bia/a4m33bia-10neuroevolution-2012.pdf)\n\n\uff08 \u4ee5\u4e0b\u3001\u4e0a\u8a18 \u30b9\u30e9\u30a4\u30c9 \u3088\u308a \u4e00\u90e8\u629c\u7c8b\u3057\u3066 \u8ee2\u8f09 \uff09\n\n![Sep20_2016.PNG](https://qiita-image-store.s3.amazonaws.com/0/43487/9af0c911-29b9-eb16-4ad2-47225b3985f3.png)\n\n\n* [\uff08 ELESVIER  \uff09J\u00fcrgen Schmidhuber, Review _Deep learning in neural networks: An overview_, Neural Networks 61 (2015) 85\u2013117](http://www2.econ.iastate.edu/tesfatsi/DeepLearningInNeuralNetworksOverview.JSchmidhuber2015.pdf)\n\n* [Jurgen Schmidhuber, _Deep Learning in Neural Networks: An Overview_](https://arxiv.org/pdf/1404.7828.pdf)\n\n> __5.3 1965: Deep Networks Based on the Group Method of Data Handling__\n\n___\n\n###__GMDH \u306b\u95a2\u3059\u308b \u30aa\u30f3\u30e9\u30a4\u30f3\u60c5\u5831__\n\n\n* [\uff08 Wikipedia \u82f1\u8a9e\u7248 \uff09_Group method of data handling_ ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Group_method_of_data_handling)\n\n> Group method of data handling (GMDH) is a family of inductive algorithms for computer-based mathematical modeling of multi-parametric datasets that features fully automatic structural and parametric optimization of models.\n>\n> GMDH is used in such fields as data mining, knowledge discovery, prediction, complex systems modeling, optimization and pattern recognition.\n\n\n* [\u7530\u6751\u5766\u4e4b\u30fb\u8fd1\u85e4\u6b63 \u300c\u89e3\u8aac \u6700\u8fd1\u306eGMDH\u306e\u65b9\u6cd5\u8ad6\u3068\u5fdc\u7528\u300d](http://www.orsj.or.jp/~archive/pdf/bul/Vol.23_02_104.pdf)\n\n* [\u6939 \u6728 \u7fa9 \u4e00, \u5c0f \u897f \u6b63 \u8eac \u300c\u65b0\u3057\u3044\u30c7\u30fc\u30bf\u51e6\u7406\u6cd5(GMDH)\u306e\u7d39\u4ecb\u3068\u305d\u306e\u88fd\u9244\u30d7\u30ed\u30bb\u30b9\u3078\u306e\u5fdc\u7528\u300d ](https://www.jstage.jst.go.jp/article/tetsutohagane1955/64/3/64_3_491/_pdf)\n\n* [\u63da \u5b50\u6c5f \u307b\u304b \u300c\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f\u975e\u7dda\u5f62\u591a\u9805\u5f0f\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb\u306e\u540c\u5b9a\u300d](http://yoh.ise.ibaraki.ac.jp/PDF/2000-2001/20080214135629.pdf)\n\n* [\u795e\u8c37 \u5c06\u53f8 \u300c\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30d7\u30ed\u30b0\u30e9\u30df\u30f3\u30b0\u3092\u7528\u3044\u305f\u6642\u7cfb\u5217\u51e6\u7406\u300d ](http://www.kochi-tech.ac.jp/library/ron/2000/info/1010383.pdf)\n\n* [\u6797 \u5149\u4e8c, \u7be0\u539f \u6176\u90a6, \u91d1\u91ce \u79c0\u654f\u300cGMDH\u306b\u57fa\u3065\u304f\u975e\u7dda\u5f62\u81ea\u5df1\u56de\u5e30\u30e2\u30c7\u30eb\u306e\u540c\u5b9a\u3068\u30b9\u30da\u30af\u30c8\u30eb\u89e3\u6790\u300d](https://www.jstage.jst.go.jp/article/sicetr1965/28/10/28_10_1216/_pdf)\n\n> __1. \u306f \u3058 \u3081 \u306b__\n>\n> GMDH (Group Method of Data Handling) \u306f1960\u5e74\u4ee3\u5f8c\u534a\u306bA. G. Ivakhnenko \u306b\u3088\u3063\u3066\u63d0\u6848\u3055\u308c\u305f\u4e00\u7a2e\u306e\u30e2\u30c7\u30ea\u30f3\u30b0\u624b\u6cd5\u3067\u3042\u308b1),2). \n>\n> \u3053\u306e\u624b\u6cd5\u306f, \u591a\u91cf\u306e\u30c7\u30fc\u30bf\u304b\u3089\u7cfb\u306e\u7279\u6027\u3092\u7cbe\u5bc6\u306b\u540c\u5b9a\u3059\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3092\u76ee\u7684\u3068\u3057\u305f\u5f93\u6765\u306e\u7d71\u8a08\u7684\u30e2\u30c7\u30ea\u30f3\u30b0\u624b\u6cd5\u3068\u306f\u7acb\u5834\u3092\u7570\u306b\u3057, \u5c11\u306a\u3044\u30c7\u30fc\u30bf\u304b\u3089\u8907\u96d1\u306a(\u975e\u7dda\u5f62)\u7cfb\u3092\u5927\u96d1\u628a\u306b\u540c\u5b9a\u3059\u308b\u3053\u3068\u3092\u76ee\u7684\u3068\u3057\u3066\u304a\u308a, \u4eca\u65e5\u306e\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30e9\u30eb\u30fb\u30cd\u30c3\u30c8\u30ef\u30fc\u30af\u306e\u539f\u578b\u3067\u3042\u308b\u30d1\u30fc\u30bb\u30d7\u30c8\u30ed\u30f3\u306e\u8003\u3048\u65b9\u3092\u30d9\u30fc\u30b9\u306b\u958b\u767a\u3057\u305f\u8a08\u7b97\u30e1\u30ab\u30cb \u30ba\u30e0 \u300c\u767a\u898b\u7684\u81ea\u5df1\u7d44\u7e54\u5316 (Heuristic Selforganization)\u300d\u3092\u7528\u3044\u3066\u3044\u308b.\n>\n> GMDH\u306f, \u63d0\u6848\u5f8c\u6570\u5e74\u3092\u7d4c\u3066\u65e5\u672c\u3067\u3082\u7814\u7a76\u304c\u59cb\u3081\u3089\u308c, 1970\u5e74\u4ee3\u306b\u306f\u6570\u591a\u304f\u306e\u7814\u7a76\u8ad6\u6587\u304c\u767a\u8868\u3055\u308c\u305f3)\uff5e5)\u304c, 1980\u5e74\u4ee3\u306b\u5165\u3063\u3066\u305d\u306e\u7814\u7a76\u71b1\u306f\u4e0b\u706b\u306b\u306a\u3063\u305f.\n\n* [GEvoM _Modelling Using GMDH-Type Neural Networks_](http://research.guilan.ac.ir/gevom/modelling_en.html)\n\n> By means of GMDH algorithm a model can be represented as set of neurons in which different pairs of them in each layer are connected through a quadratic polynomial and thus produce new neurons in the next layer. \n>\n> Such representation can be used in modelling to map inputs to outputs. \n\n* [Osman Dag and Ceylan Yozgatligil, _GMDH: An R Package for Short Term Forecasting via GMDH-Type Neural Network Algorithms_](https://journal.r-project.org/archive/2016-1/yozgatligil-dag.pdf)\n\n> __Abstract__\n>\n> Group Method of Data Handling (GMDH)-type neural network algorithms are the heuristic self organization method for the modelling of complex systems. \n>\n> GMDH algorithms are utilized for a variety of purposes, examples include identification of physical laws, the extrapolation of physical fields, pattern recognition, clustering, the approximation of multidimensional processes, forecasting without models, etc.\n>\n> In this study, the R package GMDH is presented to make short term forecasting through GMDH-type neural network algorithms. \n>\n> The GMDH package has options to use different transfer functions (sigmoid, radial basis, polynomial, and tangent functions) simultaneously or separately. \n>\n> Data on cancer death rate of Pennsylvania from 1930 to 2000 are used to illustrate the features of the GMDH package. The results based on ARIMA models and exponential smoothing methods are included for comparison.\n\n* [\uff08 ELESVIER \uff09Isa Ebtehaja _et.al, GMDH-type neural network approach for modeling the discharge coefficient of rectangular sharp-crested side weirs_](http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2215098615000774)\n\n* [Tadashi Kondo and Junji Ueno, _REVISED GMDH-TYPE NEURAL NETWORK ALGORITHM WITH A FEEDBACK LOOP IDENTIFYING SIGMOID FUNCTION NEURAL NETWORK_](http://citeseerx.ist.psu.edu/viewdoc/download?doi=10.1.1.113.5556&rep=rep1&type=pdf)\n\n* [\u8fd1\u85e4 \u6b63 ](https://www.jstage.jst.go.jp/article/sicetr1965/22/12/22_12_1283/_pdf)\n\n\n* [\u8fd1\u85e4 \u6b63 **\u305d\u3057\u3066\u3001\u30d5\u30a3\u30fc\u30c9\u30d0\u30c3\u30af\u30eb\u30fc\u30d7\u306e\u6570\u3001\u4e2d\u9593\u5c64\u306e\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30ed\u30f3\u306e\u500b\u6570\u3001\u6709\u76ca\u306a\u5165\u529b\u5909\u6570\u3001\u6700\u9069\u306a\u30cb\u30e5\u30fc\u30ed\u30f3\u69cb\u9020\u306a\u3069\u306e\u69cb\u9020\u30d1\u30e9\u30e1\u30fc\u30bf\u3092\u3001\u4e88\u6e2c\u8aa4\u5dee\u5e73\u65b9\u548c(PSS)\u3067\u5b9a\u7fa9\u3055\u308c\u305f\u4e88\u6e2c\u8aa4\u5dee\u8a55\u4fa1\u57fa\u6e96\u3092\u6700\u5c0f\u306b\u3059\u308b\u3088\u3046\u306b\u81ea\u5df1\u9078\u629e\u3059\u308b\u3002**\n>\n> \n\n\n* [\uff08 ELESVIER \uff09R. Madandousta, R. Ghavidela, N. Nariman-zadehb, _Evolutionary design of generalized GMDH-type neural network for prediction of concrete compressive strength using UPV_](http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S092702561000340X)\n\n> __Abstract__\n>\n> The main purpose of this paper is to predict the insitu compressive strength of concrete by means of non-destructive approach using ultrasonic pulse velocity (UPV) method. \n>\n> For this purpose generalized GMDH-type (group method of data handling) neural network was developed based on various data obtained experimentally. \n>\n> **Evolutionary algorithms (EAs) are deployed for optimal design of GMDH-type neural networks.**\n>\n> A set of experimental data for the training and testing the evolved GMDH-type neural network is employed in which ultrasonic pulse velocity (UPV), concrete age, water\u2013cement ratio and fine/coarse aggregate ratio are considered as inputs and concrete compressive strength is regarded as the output variables.\n>\n> Sensitivity analysis has also been carried out on one of the obtaining models to study the influence of input parameters on model output. \n>\n> The results show that generalized GMDH-type neural network has a great ability as a feasible tool for prediction of the concrete compressive strength.\n\n\n\n\n", "tags": ["\u4eba\u5de5\u77e5\u80fd", "\u5f37\u5316\u5b66\u7fd2", "\u907a\u4f1d\u7684\u30a2\u30eb\u30b4\u30ea\u30ba\u30e0", "DeepLearning", "\u6df1\u5c64\u5b66\u7fd2"]}
